  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dad3f713-4b3e-424c-be8e-c59c7fad7c22'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9305408811206345163"><i>So my only protection is a kindergarten teacher and a ninety-eight-pound female minister....And they don't even believe I'm in danger.</i> <br/> <br/> As Bethany approaches her thirteenth birthday, her parents act more oddly than usual.   <span id="freeText9305408811206345163" style="display:none"><i>So my only protection is a kindergarten teacher and a ninety-eight-pound female minister....And they don't even believe I'm in danger.</i> <br /> <br /> As Bethany approaches her thirteenth birthday, her parents act more oddly than usual. Her mother cries constantly, and her father barely lets Bethany out of his sight. Then one morning he hustles the entire family into the car, drives across several state lines -- and leaves Bethany with an aunt she never knew existed. Bethany has no idea what's going on. She's worried her mom and dad are running from some kind of trouble, but she can't find out because they won't tell her where they are going. <br /> <br /> Bethany's only clue is a few words she overheard her father tell her aunt: "She doesn't know anything about Elizabeth." But Aunt Myrlie won't tell Bethany who Elizabeth is, and she won't explain why people in her small town react to Bethany as if they've seen a ghost. The mystery intensifies when Bethany gets a package from her father containing four different birth certificates from four different states, with four different last names -- and thousands of dollars in cash. And when a strange man shows up asking questions, Bethany realizes the's not the only one who's desperate to unravel the secrets of her past.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_17790812').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

            }

          });

      $('edition_17790812').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

        });
      });

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think it was succinctly said a couple times in the book: "The truth will set you free.". She found out the truth to questions she'd been wondering a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think it was succinctly said a couple times in the book: "The truth will set you free.". She found out the truth to questions she'd been wondering about herself and her family, and in the end she let others know that truth, too. Her family came together like never before, and even the ex-con was free to live life to the fullest.<br />There is always a theme to a book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_35517969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35517969" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1046565-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243290681p2/1046565.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35517969?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/1046565-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786297023" href="/book/show/3973624-double-identity">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">preteens and teens looking for a quick, interesting read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1046565-chelsea?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35517969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5037730790037313248">I read this book in one sitting, and while I found it to be a generally enjoyable story, I think it definitely could have been better.<br/><br/>First of all, not a lot happens - we see a lot of Bethany just sitting in the house thinking. And while some pondering on the part of the main character is to be expected, that's almost all this book was. Something would happen and then Bethany would think about it, and then something else would happen and she would think about that. Her thoughts were interesting,</span>
  <span id="freeText5037730790037313248" style="display:none">I read this book in one sitting, and while I found it to be a generally enjoyable story, I think it definitely could have been better.<br /><br />First of all, not a lot happens - we see a lot of Bethany just sitting in the house thinking. And while some pondering on the part of the main character is to be expected, that's almost all this book was. Something would happen and then Bethany would think about it, and then something else would happen and she would think about that. Her thoughts were interesting, of course, but not particularly exciting, and a bit more action would have been nice (remember, this book is supposed to be an "exhilarating thriller").<br /><br />I also had some issues with the end. The pacing was okay most of the time, as they slowly revealed more and more of Bethany's true identity, but then suddenly it just... ended, and the author decided to cram the rest of the important details into the epilogue like a child cramming toys under the bed. It would have been far more interesting had other things actually, you know, <i>happened</i> that might've revealed such information instead of just saying, "Epilogue time!" and having done with it.<br /><br />The character development left a bit to be desired, as well. Dalton Van Dyne might have been a fascinating character had the author bothered to give him any development whatsoever. Instead, he got about ten pages of screen time and a random article (which hinted to me that the author was simply too bored to actually develop the character, and decided to use a cheap trick - like having someone write an article about him that the main character can then find - instead).<br /><br />All this aside, the book wasn't bad. It provoked thought - what would <i>you</i> do if you were in Bethany's situation? - and was sufficiently intriguing. The characters (aside from Van Dyne) were all very fleshed out and three-dimensional. It kept me turning pages, at least. I hardly think it constitutes an "exhilarating thriller" by any stretch of the imagination, but it was good and I would recommend it to anyone looking for a quick, enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5037730790037313248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/1567015-emma">Emma</a>

  <span id="freeText2525794122282226940" style="display:none">Bethany's parents have acted weird for as long as she can remember - making sure she's never alone, not allowing her to attend sleepovers, and generally being overprotective. What do they possibly think could happen to her?<br /><br />These actions pale in comparison to the way her parents begin to act around Bethany's thirteenth birthday. Her mother is constantly crying, for starters, and nothing Bethany says or does seems to help. This comes to a head when her parents whisk her off on a car ride to stay with an aunt she never knew she had. Her parents disappear, leaving behind unanswered questions and no number at which to contact them.<br /><br />Myrlie Walker, Bethany's aunt, finally tells her that Bethany is not an only child - her parents had another daughter - Elizabeth - who died over twenty years ago. Suddenly, Bethany realizes why people in town are staring at her as though they've seen a ghost: Bethany isn't just Elizabeth's sister - she's her clone.<br /><br />Haddix whisks the reader away into this page-turner, following Bethany as she struggles to come to terms with who she is, find her parents, and solve the mystery once and for all. </span>

<div id="review_18339176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18339176" />
    <a title="Tony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/456110-tony"><img alt="Tony" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18339176?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tony" href="/user/show/456110-tony">Tony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/456110-tony?shelf=9th-grade">9th-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18339176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3836159039082985890">Double Identity, Aladdin Paperbacks, 2005, Magaret Peterson Haddix 218 pg., $5.99, ISBN 978-0-689-87379-9<br/><br/>"Then one morning he hustles the entire family into the car, drives across several state-lines and leaves Bethany with an aunt she never knew existed, Bethany has no idea what's going on." Bethany, a modest and scared twelve year old girl, is not an ordinary person; she has an identity she can't get from other people that look at her with sorrow, having crying and worried parents that don't e</span>
  <span id="freeText3836159039082985890" style="display:none">Double Identity, Aladdin Paperbacks, 2005, Magaret Peterson Haddix 218 pg., $5.99, ISBN 978-0-689-87379-9<br /><br />"Then one morning he hustles the entire family into the car, drives across several state-lines and leaves Bethany with an aunt she never knew existed, Bethany has no idea what's going on." Bethany, a modest and scared twelve year old girl, is not an ordinary person; she has an identity she can't get from other people that look at her with sorrow, having crying and worried parents that don't explain anything about their moving and left somewhere where she doesn't feel safe. Everyone assumes she's a ghost, especially people who live 20 years ago who stayed at the same place and stare at her as if they've just seen a ghost but can't really tell if she's human. But Bethany has learned to overcome and cooperate with where she is and how people view her. As the book progresses she becomes more familiar with why she was left where she is but you'll have to read to find out what happens...<br />Imagine being an exact same twin as someone else. This is Bethany's life flipped upside down like a pizza without flavor or like a ferris wheel. This book is enough to coax you to believe something else then what your first impressions were. It impresses reader with an enhancement of beauty and it's richness of continuous events and mysteries needed to be solved. Magaret not only wants you to experience how you reveal yourself or how people view you but how important identity is to all of us. I recommend this book to anyone who enjoys fantasy or wants to learn how dangerous identity can be. <br />I vigorously enjoyed reading this juicy book. Before I started reading I thought wow a book about 2 different identities in a person...great... but it turns out that this book is impossible to put down with it's many mysteries. Margaret is an adept and a wonderful author who can make you see the world differently. It leaves readers with an identity of a character that is horrifying and haunting that's vital to not forget. It also leaves readers with many questions such as "Who am I really?" or "What's my true identity?" Go to the nearest shop and pick up this book! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3836159039082985890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_452374763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452374763" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13299299-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452374763?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/13299299-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452374763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8045174719156976532">Bethany thinks that she is an only child and normal like everyone else. The only problem is- she’s not. Weird things have happened before her big trip. Her mother is crying all the time and her father is following her everywhere she goes. She wonders, “What is happening?” Suddenly, in one day that all changes. Her parents drop her off at her Aunt Myrile’s house. She didn't even know she had an aunt! Her parents say that she will be safer there and no one will be able to find her. Bethany wonders</span>
  <span id="freeText8045174719156976532" style="display:none">Bethany thinks that she is an only child and normal like everyone else. The only problem is- she’s not. Weird things have happened before her big trip. Her mother is crying all the time and her father is following her everywhere she goes. She wonders, “What is happening?” Suddenly, in one day that all changes. Her parents drop her off at her Aunt Myrile’s house. She didn't even know she had an aunt! Her parents say that she will be safer there and no one will be able to find her. Bethany wonders-who? She feels like something bad is happening and she wants it all to stop. Then her aunt Myrile tells her news that she had never heard before. She has a twin sister and was born in four different places at the same time. Her cousin Joss tells Bethany about what it was like having Elizabeth around. Joss also tells her about what happened to Elizabeth. Everything that happened to her twin sister Elizabeth has happened to Bethany .So is Bethany really human? <br /><br />	I really recommend this book. It is like a thriller and mystery combined as one. She writes so you don’t feel like an observer, nor do you feel like Bethany. You feel like someone on the street knowing everything that is going on. You feel like a person on the street observing. <br />	I couldn’t really relate to Bethany, so it was nice that way. It’s nice sometimes to read books about other people’s lives and see what going on. If you like to relate to a character in this book, I do not recommend this book to you. I recommend this book to people who love suspense and mysteries. It isn’t like Nancy Drew with detectives; it’s like a personal mystery with Bethany and herself. <br />	I rated this book 5 stars because it was very suspenseful and different than most of the books I read. I usually can relate to the character, but this one I couldn’t. I hope that I can read more of her books during the year. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8045174719156976532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-personally-by-moi">read-personally-by-moi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21560147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer31512588779048698">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>For almost thirteen-year-old Bethany, life has suddenly and unexplicably taken a strange turn. For a girl who has never spent a night away from her parents, she's suddenly hustled into the car by her sad-looking father, subjected to listening to her sobbing mother, and unceremoniously dropped off in the middle of the night in a town she's never heard of, at the home of a woman claiming to be her Aunt Myrlie. Her parents are a lot older than her friend's parents</span>
  <span id="freeText31512588779048698" style="display:none">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />For almost thirteen-year-old Bethany, life has suddenly and unexplicably taken a strange turn. For a girl who has never spent a night away from her parents, she's suddenly hustled into the car by her sad-looking father, subjected to listening to her sobbing mother, and unceremoniously dropped off in the middle of the night in a town she's never heard of, at the home of a woman claiming to be her Aunt Myrlie. Her parents are a lot older than her friend's parents, and Bethany is sure that her parent's siblings are all dead. So who is this woman claiming to be her Aunt, and why has she never heard of her before? Why won't her mother stop crying? Why does her dad seem so eager to get away from the house in Sanderfield? And who the heck is Elizabeth, the name she overheard her father and Myrlie discussing? <br /><br />All these questions and more are only the tip of the iceberg in Margaret Peterson Haddix's newest novel, a wonderful young adult thriller that I thoroughly enjoyed. The twists and turns are unpredictable and unexpected--the conclusion one I never saw coming. <br /><br />Overall, a great suspensful read for teens and adults alike! </span>
  <a data-text-id="31512588779048698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2302927471?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Cox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Cox" href="/user/show/20064810-melissa-cox">Melissa Cox</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2302927471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16323154316433592850">I feel like if I had read this when I was like 10, I probably would have different feelings about it, but alas, that's not the case. I was incredibly BORED throughout this whole book. I had already figured everything out right after Bethany got to Sandersfield, so there really was no suspense for me, and at the end, I actually thought the explanations and everything was just kind of stupid. Also, unrealistic... If that was the bombshell dropped, there would be no peace for any of them and there </span>
  <span id="freeText16323154316433592850" style="display:none">I feel like if I had read this when I was like 10, I probably would have different feelings about it, but alas, that's not the case. I was incredibly BORED throughout this whole book. I had already figured everything out right after Bethany got to Sandersfield, so there really was no suspense for me, and at the end, I actually thought the explanations and everything was just kind of stupid. Also, unrealistic... If that was the bombshell dropped, there would be no peace for any of them and there would be lab testing out the wazzoo... but nope... it was like nothing ever happened to begin with. I just felt like this could have been done WAY BETTER with a lot more development in the story and characters. Every time something happened, we'd spend the next 10-20 pages going through Bethany's thoughts on the whole thing... that was basically the whole book. All of the exciting stuff (if you want to call it that) happened at the very end, and by then, I was so over it all, that I really didn't care.<br /><br />Again, I think if I was 10, this probably would have been different for me... which is why I gave it 2 stars instead of one... that extra star is my own guess that I probably really would have enjoyed this if I was a clueless kid with limited reading experience, but since I am not, I didn't really like it all that much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16323154316433592850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_729109665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729109665" />
    <a title="Aysia Schroeder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23661963-aysia-schroeder"><img alt="Aysia Schroeder" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/729109665?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aysia Schroeder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aysia Schroeder" href="/user/show/23661963-aysia-schroeder">Aysia Schroeder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729109665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5084783175843813968"> The book, "Double Identity", is told by a 12 year old girl named Bethany. Bethany thinks she is an average girl with two parents, and gets anything she wants. She loves to swim and come up with big words that no one will understand. Not everything is as normal as it seems to the outside world. Bethany’s Mom, Hillary cries every single day and Bethany has no idea why. Everything changes when one day her parents put her in the car and drive for hours. They drop her off at her Aunt Myrlie’s house,</span>
  <span id="freeText5084783175843813968" style="display:none"> The book, "Double Identity", is told by a 12 year old girl named Bethany. Bethany thinks she is an average girl with two parents, and gets anything she wants. She loves to swim and come up with big words that no one will understand. Not everything is as normal as it seems to the outside world. Bethany’s Mom, Hillary cries every single day and Bethany has no idea why. Everything changes when one day her parents put her in the car and drive for hours. They drop her off at her Aunt Myrlie’s house, an aunt she didn’t even know existed. They leave her there and don’t tell her where they’re going, or why. Bethany is not allowed to call and is to stay by her Aunt’s side at all times. Soon Bethany comes to find out why everyone in Saunderfield, Illinois looks at her so differently and that she is in fact, not an original like everyone else in the world is. <br /><br />	Bethany is 12 years old and definitely acts like she’s 16. She thinks she needs to be apart of everything that is going on that no one should treat her like she’s just a child. There are a few times that she does act like one, like when she throws a tantrum that she wants her parents back. Aunt Myrlie is just a normal older woman. She’s a kindergarten teacher with one daughter and a dead husband. Elizabeth is Bethany’s sister. Although she may be dead, she is still a very important part of the story and as you read you will learn I don’t need to share a lot about Elizabeth because anything I have told you about Bethany, sums up Elizabeth. <br /><br />	The setting of the story mostly takes place in Saunderfield, Illinois.This is very important because this is where Bethany’s parents grew up and also raised Elizabeth. The setting of this story is everything about the story because none of the pieces would have fell together if it did not take place here.<br /><br /> I think the theme in this story is to show that there are a lot of things in this world that are unknown. Things from people's past that we would never guess happened. <br />	<br />I recommend this book to anyone who likes a good mystery. It will really make you think about the possibilities of the outcome. This book is suitable for 7th graders and above. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5084783175843813968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_80611770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80611770" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3018990-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1260219346p2/3018990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80611770?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/3018990-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786297023" href="/book/show/3973624-double-identity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80611770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10300574960855104719"><u> Double Identity </u> is a very good book. It has a twisty plot, but it’s very interesting. Bethany and her parents seem to be in a great deal of danger. She is very curious. Her parents take her to stay with an aunt that she has never heard of before. Her life before this situation was perfect. She was spoiled, home schooled, and got whatever she wanted. Her parents were very protective, and know they just leave her with someone she has never met. She wants to know what is going on, but there is no</span>
  <span id="freeText10300574960855104719" style="display:none"><u> Double Identity </u> is a very good book. It has a twisty plot, but it’s very interesting. Bethany and her parents seem to be in a great deal of danger. She is very curious. Her parents take her to stay with an aunt that she has never heard of before. Her life before this situation was perfect. She was spoiled, home schooled, and got whatever she wanted. Her parents were very protective, and know they just leave her with someone she has never met. She wants to know what is going on, but there is no one for her to talk to, and she has no way of getting in touch with her father. Throughout this book, I was curious as well. I wanted to know why her parents were acting so strange, and who this Myrlie is. I wanted to know who Elizabeth was, and why it was all such a secret. This book is full of fear, trust, and life-changing situations. I loved the suspense as I read, and it made me actually want to read it. It is interesting to think that this could be a real-life situation. This book really made me think, and kept me interested. The lesson that I got from it, was the fact that you should be yourself no matter what. Bethany did not know what was happening, but she stood strong and never gave up. As many questions as she had for Myrlie, she did not ask and she was never rude. She trusted her, and she had faith, that her parents would do everything that they could possibly do, to keep her safe. At first the story was slow, but before too long I was hooked. I usually don’t read, but I really enjoyed this book. It kept me wondering, and I really seemed to connect with Bethany. I would recommend this book for any teen; boy or girl. I think adults would enjoy it, as well. It is full of thrills, and a question is being answered non-stop. The end of the book was not what I expected but it was okay. Elizabeth turned out to be someone that I never imagined. The whole time I was reading, I was thinking of all the possibilities. Nothing seemed to turn out like I thought it would, but it was good. The idea of “being yourself” stuck throughout the whole book. Anyone who reads this, will definitely be curious, and ask many questions. If you like mysteries and suspenseful stories, this is the book for you. In the end, I was just as surprised as Bethany was and throughout the book, and was just as confused as she was! All of her questions were answered, and everything fell into place. I can not wait to read another book by Haddix, and I hope that I will be just as satisfied. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10300574960855104719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1777550464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777550464" />
    <a title="Abril Cervantes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60325808-abril-cervantes"><img alt="Abril Cervantes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475783962p2/60325808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777550464?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abril Cervantes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abril Cervantes" href="/user/show/60325808-abril-cervantes">Abril Cervantes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777550464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17430360715508670363"> "Double Identity" by Margaret Peterson Haddix is a mystery book that has its good and bad things. It has some plot twists that leave the reader wanting to find out what happens. <br/> <br/> The book starts out with Bethany, the main character, on a drive to visit an aunt she didn't even know existed. Her mom has been crying the whole ride there and she is shocked when her parents tell her that they are leaving her with this aunt. Her mysterious aunt is then introduced as her aunt Myrlie. Bethany’s dad ca</span>
  <span id="freeText17430360715508670363" style="display:none"> "Double Identity" by Margaret Peterson Haddix is a mystery book that has its good and bad things. It has some plot twists that leave the reader wanting to find out what happens. <br /> <br /> The book starts out with Bethany, the main character, on a drive to visit an aunt she didn't even know existed. Her mom has been crying the whole ride there and she is shocked when her parents tell her that they are leaving her with this aunt. Her mysterious aunt is then introduced as her aunt Myrlie. Bethany’s dad calls once a day, but his number can’t be tracked and Bethany has no idea what’s going on. She starts hearing the name of a girl named Elizabeth, and so many people start staring at her and asking if she really is Elizabeth, that she no longer wants to go out in public. She's desperate to find out who Elizabeth is and what her family was been keeping from her for such a long time.<br /> <br /> *Spoiler* I think that the title "Double Identity" relates to the book and it's plot well because when Bethany found out that she was actually a clone of her deceased sister, Elizabeth, she learns about this whole different side of herself, almost like she had a double identity this whole time. In the book, the line "the truth will set you free" , and I believe that this is the theme. This theme can be seen when she found out the truth to questions she'd been wondering about herself and her family, and in the end she let others know that truth about herself too. Her family came together like never before, and even the "bad guy" was able to be set free and go on with his life, <br /> <br /> In my opinion , this was good book but a lot of things could have been better. This story lacked the action it had potential for. The whole book is mostly about Bethany wondering about who she is, but she never really does anything about it. The main I liked about this were the characters because you could tell as the reader that they all genuinely cared about each other. I liked the way the author brought her family all together at the end and everything was peaceful but there could've been a lot more action. <br /> <br /> On the scale of 1-5 , I would rate this book a 3.5 because like I said, it could've been more intense, especially towards the end. I would recommend this book to anyone who likes mysteries that aren't really severe. Overall, I think this book is decent but it isn't something I wouldn't say it's one of my favorites. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17430360715508670363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14275596506925013536">I'd like to start by saying that this book didn't really do anything for me proving why I rated it thusly. That being said it was a cute story about a girl who is dropped off at her aunt's house that she had no knowledge of and her parents take off leaving her in this unknown woman's care.   <span id="freeText14275596506925013536" style="display:none">I'd like to start by saying that this book didn't really do anything for me proving why I rated it thusly. That being said it was a cute story about a girl who is dropped off at her aunt's house that she had no knowledge of and her parents take off leaving her in this unknown woman's care. Bethany the little girl is left dumbfounded how her perfect family was ripped to pieces in a matter of moments. Bethany's aunt lets slip that she looks like a girl named Elizbeth who has some sort of connection with Bethany. Later on, we discover that there is some sort of relationship between these two girls that furthers Bethany's struggle in life as she discovers who she is and why her parents have marooned her on the island of aunt nobody. I would think despite my opinion of this book as a whole I'd love to use this book to show how great dialogue can lead a story forward and develop characters without the use of multiple life changing events. </span>

  <span id="freeText17443114760029512180" style="display:none">This is one of my favorites! It involves a great mystery with a little science. I thought I had it figured out until I found out the real truth, and I was shocked! Great page turner!<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Summary:</b>
</u>As the novel opens, Bethany is anxious; her father has barely let her out of his sight and her mother has been weeping for months. Now, a few days before her 13th birthday, her father has put the two of them in the car, headed West. He leaves Bethany with her Aunt Myrlie and drives off with no explanation. The only clue Bethany has is what she heard her father say to her aunt, "She doesn't know anything about Elizabeth." Bethany is determined to learn why she has been left with an aunt she never knew existed, and what the mysterious Elizabeth has to do with it all.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2215146468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215146468" />
    <a title="Rylee Diamond" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59397922-rylee-diamond"><img alt="Rylee Diamond" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2215146468?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rylee Diamond" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rylee Diamond" href="/user/show/59397922-rylee-diamond">Rylee Diamond</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215146468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18128165342334952793">I read the book Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix. The characters in this book are Bethany, Myrlie, Joss, the mom (whose name is not mentioned) the dad (David), Dalton Van Dyne, Bridgie and Elizabeth. In this book Bethany’s mom cries and cries and cries. One day Bethany’s parents tell her to get in the car and Bethany listens. They drive for a very long time and when Bethany asks where they are going the only answer she gets is her mother’s non-stop crying. When the car comes to a stop</span>
  <span id="freeText18128165342334952793" style="display:none">I read the book Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix. The characters in this book are Bethany, Myrlie, Joss, the mom (whose name is not mentioned) the dad (David), Dalton Van Dyne, Bridgie and Elizabeth. In this book Bethany’s mom cries and cries and cries. One day Bethany’s parents tell her to get in the car and Bethany listens. They drive for a very long time and when Bethany asks where they are going the only answer she gets is her mother’s non-stop crying. When the car comes to a stop Bethany is dropped off at her aunt’s house that she does not really know. While Bethany is staying at her aunt’s house (Myrlie) and her daughter (Joss) Bethany finds out about a sister. Not a sister that Joss has or a sister that Myrlie has but a sister that Bethany has. Bethany is in shock. She has a sister that died before she was born and she just barely found out about her. Now something mysterious and strange happens. Bethanys dad sends a bunch of birth certificates and thousands of dollars of cash. Bethany takes a look at the birth certificates and she sees that they all have her name on them. All 4 of these birth certificates have her name on it but a different last name and different state on every single one of them. Bethany is very confused and wants to know what is going on. With all of these strange things there is a letter from David saying how he is being hunted. Bethany wants to find out who is hunting her dad and why. <br /><br />I thought that this book was very good and interesting. It didn’t have many parts that were unnecessary because every part of the book contributed to the overall story that is going on. I don’t regret reading this book because I don’t usually enjoy reading but this was very good and made me want to read and made reading more enjoyable for me. I liked pretty much everything because it was very detailed and it helped me understand it more. I do agree with the author’s perspective. I can’t connect to this book because it was not very real. I can connect because Bethany has a sister and I have 2 sisters. But she didn’t know about her sister and I know about my sisters. The voice of the character matters because she tells how she feels about what is going on with her and her life and if she wasn’t saying how she felt it would be harder to understand because the readers wouldn’t know and wouldn’t be able to relate to her. <br /><br />	The point that the author is trying to convey wasn’t very clear to me but if I had to guess at what it is it could that if you’re curious about someone or something to find out what it is and don’t let people walk all over you. In this book Bethany says, “I can’t believe my parents have hid this from me for so long but now i must find out what else they are hiding”. This is proving my point because Bethany is saying that she must find out what else her parents are hiding and shes not going to stop. I think that the author could have made the message he is sending more clear but I think it is also good because since he didn’t make it very clear it makes people have to think more about what the message is instead of it being obvious. So overall the message of this story is to solve your curiosity. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18128165342334952793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5475687206258789825">In the novel “Double Identity” by Margaret Peterson Haddix, Bethany, a 12 year old girl faces the challenges of her parents who are slightly older than most of the parents of her friends being over protective. Bethany’s mom will not stop crying and her dad is acting super weird around her. They are going on a super long road trip and her parents will not tell her where they are going. All of a sudden, they pull up into a driveway of an unknown town, and an unknown neighborhood that Bethany had n</span>
  <span id="freeText5475687206258789825" style="display:none">In the novel “Double Identity” by Margaret Peterson Haddix, Bethany, a 12 year old girl faces the challenges of her parents who are slightly older than most of the parents of her friends being over protective. Bethany’s mom will not stop crying and her dad is acting super weird around her. They are going on a super long road trip and her parents will not tell her where they are going. All of a sudden, they pull up into a driveway of an unknown town, and an unknown neighborhood that Bethany had never been to before. Her dad unloads her out of the car with her suitcase and told the unfamiliar old woman named Myrlie to take good care of Bethany until they get back. Little did Bethany know , her parents would not be returning to get her anytime soon. It turns out that Myrlie was Bethany’s mothers sister which made Myrlie her aunt. This experience mad Bethany wonder about her whole life, whether it was a whole big lie or a whole big truth. When Bethany went to the Y for a swim in the pool with Myrlie, a woman looked at her and said you look exactly like someone I knew years and years and years ago. It made Bethany wonder even more. Little did Bethany know, her parents had had a daughter named Elizabeth years ago when they were young and Bethany looked like a clone of Elizabeth. Elizabeth died the day she turned thirteen years old. It was so tragic and that’s why her parents were so over protective towards Bethany. It also turned out that Bethany had tons of different last names and it was so bizarre to everyone because Myrlie knew Bethany’s dad as Walter Krull and Bethany’s last name was Cole, it made Bethany wonder once again. Bethany was in danger and she didn’t even know it. Everywhere she went everyone would stare at her in astonishment and tell her that she looked like someone that they knew years upon years upon years ago. And they couldn’t take their eyes off of Bethany. It was the strangest experience that Bethany had ever had in her entire life. Bethany was most worried about her parents when the sent her ten thousand dollars through the mail and there was no return address on the envelope. They tried to redial phone calls from Walter but there was no answer and all the phone would say was. This number is incorrect. Something astonishing happens at the end but I shall not reveal</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19291001-jaina-rose?shelf=blogged">blogged</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19291001-jaina-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586719594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1703608625959270502">I have read every single book by Margaret Peterson Haddix, and this book is still one of my absolute favorites, a reading stand-by that never gets old.<br/>Bethany's parents put her in the car, drive for days, and won't answer any of her questions about what's going on. Her mother has been crying for no apparant reason for the past few months. She's frightened, and doesn't know what's going on with the parents who usually take such good care of their one and only darling. Then they drop her off at a </span>
  <span id="freeText1703608625959270502" style="display:none">I have read every single book by Margaret Peterson Haddix, and this book is still one of my absolute favorites, a reading stand-by that never gets old.<br />Bethany's parents put her in the car, drive for days, and won't answer any of her questions about what's going on. Her mother has been crying for no apparant reason for the past few months. She's frightened, and doesn't know what's going on with the parents who usually take such good care of their one and only darling. Then they drop her off at a house with a woman claiming to be her Aunt Myrlie, without saying when they'll be back. She must learn what is going on with her parents, and why everyone who sees her acts like she's supposed to be dead (note: not a living-dead book! Thought I should say that . . . ), and who is this Elizabeth she heard her father mention to Myrlie (i.e. "she doesn't know anything about Elizabeth")? Also, who is the man who seems to almost be stalking her, and what does he want with her parents? Bethany struggles to find answers, but the more she gets the more she doesn't know if she really wants to know the answer to her questions.<br />I've read this book at least five times, and I know the big ending. I still love to read it anyway. The characters are lovingly crafted and engaging, big questions are raised, and I just love the big advice theme in the novel - Don't ask why did something happen, just ask what you're going to do next. I totally reccomend this to any and all who are considering it, I think it might technically be called a thriller ('m not clear on that, thought), but it is very appropriate, the violence is practically nonexistant, and the main struggle is a phsycological one. A wonderful book all around, and maybe you'll even consider picking up one of her other books! <br />This review is also on my blog, at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ireadtilldawn.blogspot.com/2014/01/double-identity-by-margaret-peterson.html">http://ireadtilldawn.blogspot.com/201...</a>.<br /><br />If you're looking for other books by this author, I reccomend the Missing Series, or the Shadow Children books. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/303073.Escape_from_Memory" title="Escape from Memory by Margaret Peterson Haddix" rel="nofollow noopener">Escape from Memory</a> is another good stand-alone you might like if you like this one.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5012420441952279597">I started the book and I loved it because this book showed suspense. The first sentence that the book started with was "My mother is crying." The first thing I thought was "Why is she crying?" The more that I read the more I had understood why she was crying. The main character in Double Identity is Bethany who is about to turn thirteen. In the beginning of the book her parents take her to her aunt Myrlie. Bethany never knew she had a aunt so she was confused. Every time Bethany would ask a ques</span>
  <span id="freeText5012420441952279597" style="display:none">I started the book and I loved it because this book showed suspense. The first sentence that the book started with was "My mother is crying." The first thing I thought was "Why is she crying?" The more that I read the more I had understood why she was crying. The main character in Double Identity is Bethany who is about to turn thirteen. In the beginning of the book her parents take her to her aunt Myrlie. Bethany never knew she had a aunt so she was confused. Every time Bethany would ask a question, Myrlie would pause and not finish answering the question. She would hear Myrlie and her father talking about a girl named Elizabeth. <br /><br />Who is a Elizabeth? Bethany wanted to know so bad but she didn't know how to find out. Myrlie wouldn't talk to her about it because she would always pause. One night it was about 2:00 am and Bethany heard the phone ring. She got right out b of bed and answered the phone. It was her mom. Her mom screams in the phone "Elizabeth?" She was kind if confused because she has been trying to figure out who she is. Her mother tells Bethany on the phone that she had this horrible dream about her birthday at Sinclair Mountain. Her dad then grabs the phone and she just keeps screaming Elizabeth. Her father told Myrlie to tell her about Elizabeth.<br /><br />Elizabeth was 13 years old when she died. She had a cousin Joss who is still alive. They were best of friends. They both loved the Olympics. On the way to the Olympics, they got in a car crash. Bethany's mom blames herself for the accident. Later on in the book Bethany meets Joss and she brings over a bunch of videos with Elizabeth. Bethany and Elizabeth look a little similar. At the end of the book her parents come back and they all end up changing. They see Myrlie more often.<br /><br />I loved this book. It was so good! The beginning blew me away because I didn't think this book would be so great. This is the first book that I have read from the Author Haddix. She is now my favorite author because all of her books start with suspense and you cannot put her books down because they are so amazing! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naylea Mora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naylea Mora" href="/user/show/34845714-naylea-mora">Naylea Mora</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190951921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11074205670684959836">***SPOILER ALERT*** Do you like books about mystery? Then this is the perfect book for you. The Genre of this book is mystery. I thought this book was very interesting and when you stopped reading this book left you on edge like "What's going to happen next?". <br/> <br/> The main character is a girl named Bethany whose life is turned upside down when her parents unexpectantly take her to her " aunt's " house who she has never heard of before. The setting of this book is at Bethany"s aunt Myrlie's house. </span>
  <span id="freeText11074205670684959836" style="display:none">***SPOILER ALERT*** Do you like books about mystery? Then this is the perfect book for you. The Genre of this book is mystery. I thought this book was very interesting and when you stopped reading this book left you on edge like "What's going to happen next?". <br /> <br /> The main character is a girl named Bethany whose life is turned upside down when her parents unexpectantly take her to her " aunt's " house who she has never heard of before. The setting of this book is at Bethany"s aunt Myrlie's house. Bethany has a sister named Elizabeth who died in a car crash before Bethany was born. The type of conflict in this book is person vs. person because Bethany has to fight the " mystery man " who is after her father.<br /> <br /> I was surprised when Bethany found out she was a clone of her sister Elizabeth because what kind of parent would clone their dead daughter just because she's gone and they want her back. That is just crazy that her parents would do that. I was shocked when Bethany found out that the mystery man that was stalking her turned out not to be a bad guy because I really, truly, thought that he was going to do something to Bethany and her father.<br /> <br /> " Double Identity" is a good title for this book because when Bethany found out she was a clone she didn't feel like "Bethany" she felt like "Bethany" didn't exist and that she was Elizabeth. I was angry when her parents didn't call Bethany because she didn't know what to do with know one to guide her.<br /> <br /> On a scale of 1 star to 5 stars, I would give this book 5 stars because it really made me want to keep reading and never put the book down. I would recommend this book to people who like mysteries or sic fi books. "Double Identity" was a great book to read and it will leave you feeling on edge. Maybe in the future cloning might become a thing.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmineehs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmineehs" href="/user/show/6639367-jasmineehs">Jasmineehs</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243299648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2245017236182668537">I read Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix. The main characters in this book are 13 year old Bethany, Her aunt Myrlie and Bethany’s dead sister Elizabeth. The characters in the book are very well told and explained. The author gives great detail about each character, you feel as if you really know them by the end of the book. Bethany comes off like any other teenage girl, a little shy but no abnormal. Elizabeth on the other hand was totally out there. She was outgoing and into sports. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText2245017236182668537" style="display:none">I read Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix. The main characters in this book are 13 year old Bethany, Her aunt Myrlie and Bethany’s dead sister Elizabeth. The characters in the book are very well told and explained. The author gives great detail about each character, you feel as if you really know them by the end of the book. Bethany comes off like any other teenage girl, a little shy but no abnormal. Elizabeth on the other hand was totally out there. She was outgoing and into sports. The characters in this book were very well rounded and unique.<br />I am not sure how realistic the plot was but that what made it the page turner that it is. What happens in the book you feel like no way this is crazy, and it keeps you going. When I read this book I could not put it down to save my life. There are probably three twists in total in the book. They are pretty straight forward. The last twist is not fully understood until the very end of the book. The book moved very fast and I loved It, I can’t stand when a book moves too slowly.<br />The book had very short paragraphs, it made me feel like I was flying through this book and making a lot of progress. I really enjoyed the author’s style of writing with the short paragraphs. The author made the book exciting and funny all at the same time. The writing was relatable with friendships and how things can go wrong in a matter of seconds, and the rest of your life can be altered. I think that the author might have been trying too hard with this book, on the other hand it worked the book overall was amazing, it couldn’t of been better.<br /></span>

<div id="review_307413638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307413638" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6301306-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307413638?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/6301306-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6301306-laura?shelf=finished-irp-books">finished-irp-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6301306-laura?shelf=double-identity">double-identity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307413638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5016235733322695862">Double Identity by Margaret Peterson is about A 12 year old girl named Bethany. Her parents begin to worry about her as her thirteen birthday is coming. One night, they decide to take her to a woman’s house who she later finds belongs is her Aunt. A while passes and Bethany doesn’t hear anything from her parents that gives her any detail as to why she was left there. Then, she receives a mysterious call from her mother. She says, “I’m not supposed to call you, you know. I just wanted to talk to </span>
  <span id="freeText5016235733322695862" style="display:none">Double Identity by Margaret Peterson is about A 12 year old girl named Bethany. Her parents begin to worry about her as her thirteen birthday is coming. One night, they decide to take her to a woman’s house who she later finds belongs is her Aunt. A while passes and Bethany doesn’t hear anything from her parents that gives her any detail as to why she was left there. Then, she receives a mysterious call from her mother. She says, “I’m not supposed to call you, you know. I just wanted to talk to Elizabeth”(Haddix 124). Her mother thinks she is talking to Elizabeth, but she’s not. Although, Bethany decides to continue the conversation, and she finds out more than she wants to know. <br />	This book was actually really interesting to me. It was suspenseful and each page made me want to keep reading. I liked how it wasn’t too short, and how it wasn’t too long. Even though the book was told by a 13 year old girl the author created her as an intelligent person, with a expanded vocabulary, and there were also funny parts too just because of the way she talked. There was a lot of detail and it was easy to keep up with.<br />	I would give this book 5. I really enjoyed how it was somewhat of a challenge and how it was suspenseful. The last book I read was boring but I wanted to keep reading to see if there would be a change in plot, and there wasn’t. The ending was good because there was an epilogue at the end and it cleared everything up, and I liked the quote at the ending. It said “For my tree, I chose a ginkgo: a tree that’s unique, with an unusual history. A tree that’s survived against the odds. Like me” (Haddix 218).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5016235733322695862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1126838437" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126838437" />
    <a title="Sharupa Azmal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35456896-sharupa-azmal"><img alt="Sharupa Azmal" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1126838437?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharupa Azmal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharupa Azmal" href="/user/show/35456896-sharupa-azmal">Sharupa Azmal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126838437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13406249269083356459">The book Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix is extremely enthralling and intriguing. Bethany just lives her life as a normal girl until she slowly nears to her 13th birthday. So much is going on because she suddenly realizes who she really is and unravels an entire mystery about her life and what happened before she was even born. The way that Margaret presents this story is totally in a different style than most books are written. She decides to combine a little bit of science with mys</span>
  <span id="freeText13406249269083356459" style="display:none">The book Double Identity by Margaret Peterson Haddix is extremely enthralling and intriguing. Bethany just lives her life as a normal girl until she slowly nears to her 13th birthday. So much is going on because she suddenly realizes who she really is and unravels an entire mystery about her life and what happened before she was even born. The way that Margaret presents this story is totally in a different style than most books are written. She decides to combine a little bit of science with mystery that creates this whole new plot that is so exhilarating. The fact that she was able to make the beginning interesting too I applaud her for that since its really hard to grasp the readers attention in the first page and most authors are not really used to doing that. She creates so many twists and turns in this story that it is really hard just to not read the book. The ending of the story showed a really true and intense meaning about the entire book. It shows so much irony in a way since in the beginning the tone and mood were set a specific way but now when you come to the end it gives you a true satisfaction of what a perfect ending is rather than those so called “ HAPPILY EVER AFTER.“ Even though this book doesn’t relate to me in any way i still love it since it made me thought that if I were Bethany would I be reacting the same way as her or not. So this book provides you with a good story and it gives you a deep understanding of what you would feel like if you were this character and it really shows so much that its hard to describe in words. This book is such a thriller that you would obviously never been able to put it down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13406249269083356459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1454945157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454945157" />
    <a title="Denise Peng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47115154-denise-peng"><img alt="Denise Peng" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1454945157?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise Peng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise Peng" href="/user/show/47115154-denise-peng">Denise Peng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454945157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12278159134211362412">I enjoyed this book a lot! I really liked the theme of this which was 'Truth will set you free' which was said a few times in the book. The main character in this book is Bethany who is almost turning 13 years old and kids around that age would like this because you could see how it felt for Bethany at this age. Everything in her life has changed for her and her future is unclear. She has to put her future together piece by piece in order to find answers to all her questions because her parents </span>
  <span id="freeText12278159134211362412" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book a lot! I really liked the theme of this which was 'Truth will set you free' which was said a few times in the book. The main character in this book is Bethany who is almost turning 13 years old and kids around that age would like this because you could see how it felt for Bethany at this age. Everything in her life has changed for her and her future is unclear. She has to put her future together piece by piece in order to find answers to all her questions because her parents drove off without her leaving her to wonder about what was happening. This is a mystery book with a little science so I would recommend this to mystery and science fiction lovers. Just as I thought I knew the truth, the actual truth about what was happening in the book shocked me. The whole time I was reading this, I thought "What's going to happen next?". This story leaves you on the edge of your seat and there was so much suspense in the book. It was honestly an amazing book because I love these types of books. This title dragged me in because the title 'Double Identity' sounded really interesting and I was right; it was really interesting and it was full of adventure. This book was really well-paced with well described details. This book was like a rollercoaster full of twists and turns that dragged me in from the very beginning until the very end. The plot was interesting, the characters were well developed and everything in the book just made it so enjoyable. It's a great page-turner! Out of 5 stars, I'd give it 5 stars because it was a fun read with all the elements of a good book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12278159134211362412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76705047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8486905914827922518">I love this book. It has mystery, adventure and scary all mixed up in it. You won't be able to put this book down!! When I read the first couple of pages I hated this book! After I read more and more I started to really like it after that. This book is about a 13 year old girl, Bethany, who has had some trouble and ended up staying with her Aunt she never even knew exsisted. Now she has to find all of the pieces and put them together to seek her future before a criminal does it for her. <br/><br/>I recomm</span>
  <span id="freeText8486905914827922518" style="display:none">I love this book. It has mystery, adventure and scary all mixed up in it. You won't be able to put this book down!! When I read the first couple of pages I hated this book! After I read more and more I started to really like it after that. This book is about a 13 year old girl, Bethany, who has had some trouble and ended up staying with her Aunt she never even knew exsisted. Now she has to find all of the pieces and put them together to seek her future before a criminal does it for her. <br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who loves a great mystery! It has suspense/thriller, comedy, horror and all sorts of stuff are in this book. Now everybody is remembering her from some sort of past she may have had. Her Aunt won't tell her what's going on, her Aunt's daughter Jess won't say a word, after every stranger she talks to who said Bethany is Elizabeth, she starts to wonder if this Elizabeth could be her twin sister that died in a car wreck. <br /><br />Will she find out what really happened to her and will she ever know what her real name is? You have to read the book to find out. This book is by Margaret Peterson Haddix, and for me it was so much fun reading this because you never know if the guy is the criminal or if the criminal is really her dad that worked with him a long time ago to create Bethany who is really a robot? You won't know unitl the end.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1PqHpcQn1YlxtnJTh7xngW1z4Zb3urFmsdgauFKjd4c4t5CiPtEHaUuo735meh8ibpeO8zz/kPz4QEhL+GxF0w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KwJY51qvzUc0dKVC2gYAr+UKt0NR/RbU7TAXS7m9px/HT0/goFkfpw5qOG87wHgM5u7YJpq4N06kqEW4E3KVSw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix">About Margaret Peterson Haddix</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1309842407p3/14617.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix">Margaret Peterson Haddix
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,252
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11760030474445267376">Margaret Peterson Haddix grew up on a farm near Washington Court House, Ohio. She graduated from Miami University (of Ohio) with degrees in English/journalism, English/creative writing and history. Before her first book was published, she worked as a newspaper copy editor in Fort Wayne, Indiana; a newspaper reporter in Indianapolis; and a community college instructor and freelance writer in Danvil</span>
  <span id="freeText11760030474445267376" style="display:none">Margaret Peterson Haddix grew up on a farm near Washington Court House, Ohio. She graduated from Miami University (of Ohio) with degrees in English/journalism, English/creative writing and history. Before her first book was published, she worked as a newspaper copy editor in Fort Wayne, Indiana; a newspaper reporter in Indianapolis; and a community college instructor and freelance writer in Danville, Illinois. <br /><br /> She has since written more than 25 books for kids and teens, including <i>Running Out of Time</i>; <i>Don’t You Dare Read This, Mrs. Dunphrey</i>; <i>Leaving Fishers</i>; <i>Just Ella</i>; <i>Turnabout</i>; <i>Takeoffs and Landings</i>; <i>The Girl with 500 Middle Names</i>; <i>Because of Anya</i>; <i>Escape from Memory</i>; <i>Say What?</i>; <i>The House on the Gulf</i>; <i>Double Identity</i>; <i>Dexter the Tough</i>; <i>Uprising</i>; <i>Palace of Mirrors</i>; <i>Claim to Fame</i>; the <i>Shadow Children</i> series; and the <i>Missing</i> series. She also wrote <i>Into the Gauntlet</i>, the tenth book in the <i>39 Clues</i> series. Her books have been honored with <i>New York Times</i> bestseller status, the International Reading Association’s Children’s Book Award; American Library Association Best Book and Quick Pick for Reluctant Young Adult Readers notations; and more than a dozen state reader’s choice awards.<br /><br /><br /> Haddix and her husband, Doug, now live in Columbus, Ohio, with their two children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11760030474445267376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
